  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_674c7886-e619-46f7-a2ee-577b4324d420'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer5697350416424914896">Woods had his perfect life mapped out for him. Rise up the ranks of the family business. Marry the rich girl of his parents’ dreams.   <span id="freeText5697350416424914896" style="display:none">Woods had his perfect life mapped out for him. Rise up the ranks of the family business. Marry the rich girl of his parents’ dreams. Pretend that wealth and privilege was all he’d ever wanted. Then a girl named Della breezed into town, a beautifully imperfect stranger who captured his heart and opened his eyes to a new kind of future. Woods is ready and willing to sacrifice everything for her when the sudden death of his father leaves him with his mother to care for and a business to manage.<br /><br />Della is determined to be strong for Woods, even as she’s quietly falling to pieces. No matter how far from home she’s run, the ghosts of her past have never stopped haunting her. Struggling to hide her true feelings from Woods, Della fears she can’t be his rock without dragging him down into the darkness with her. But is she strong enough to let go of the last thing holding her together?</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_19027602').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_19027602').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;

            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_19027602').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {

        });

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_730267776" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/730267776" />
    <a title="Geri Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11757728-geri-reads"><img alt="Geri Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487874758p2/11757728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/730267776?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Geri Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Geri Reads" href="/user/show/11757728-geri-reads">Geri Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476756523" href="/book/show/18051070-simple-perfection">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer730267776" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1266362839866188667"><b>1.5 rounded off to 2 disappointing stars!!</b><br/><br/>Where do I even start with this review? <br/><br/><a href='http://tinypic.com?ref=vos7dt' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380738873ra/3117512.gif' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I think I may have to apologize in advance to anyone who might find this review/rant offensive. Nothing against Abbi Glines really. I have loved some of her books in the past and I think she pretty much got herself a sweet slice of the NA pie genre. But that said, this book was such a disappointment for me.<br/><br/><a href='http://tinypic.com?ref=315jvvs' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380738873ra/3117513.gif' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Simple Perfection starts off where Twisted Perfection left off with Woods dealing with the death of hi</span>
  <span id="freeText1266362839866188667" style="display:none"><b>1.5 rounded off to 2 disappointing stars!!</b><br><br>Where do I even start with this review? <br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=vos7dt" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380738873ra/3117512.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I think I may have to apologize in advance to anyone who might find this review/rant offensive. Nothing against Abbi Glines really. I have loved some of her books in the past and I think she pretty much got herself a sweet slice of the NA pie genre. But that said, this book was such a disappointment for me.<br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=315jvvs" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380738873ra/3117513.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Simple Perfection starts off where Twisted Perfection left off with Woods dealing with the death of his father and its aftermath. Della, while far from totally being healed from her night terrors, is coping with Woods by her side. Woods is now the sole owner of the Kerrington Club, one that his grandfather had always meant to be for him. With that comes the added responsibility of dealing with his mother and of course, Angelina. <br><br>*Sigh*<br><br>Angelina, the bitch from hell. I should focus my hatred on her but surprisingly enough, aside from that "encounter" with Della during the first half of the book, she pretty much disappeared the second half. Yeah, I can't believe it myself. I thought for sure Ms. Glines would try and milk that to the hilt ala Nan circa Too Far Series, but she didn't. <br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=24dlzle" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380738873ra/3117514.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Just as I was about to breathe a sigh of relief, this BIG MISUNDERSTANDING happened. One of my most hated plot device ever, second only that other plot device that happened at 86%. It's like the author was saying, "Hmm, wait a minute. I've written myself into a corner. There's no more conflict to keep the story going, let me throw in some epic "BIG MISUNDERSTANDING" right here." Boo-f*ckin'-hoo. Guess what? It didn't work. It just made me hate Della more. Yes, more. <br><br>There, I said it. There is a thin line between a heroine who, because of the circumstances that happened in her life, is vulnerable and a WEAK heroine. Della, I'm sorry to say, is just a weak heroine. She got better towards the end but more than of half of the book she was just whiny and pathetic. You want to find yourself and you don't want to be a burden? Great! Wonderful! That's totally understandable! But by God, if you truly wanted to find yourself and be self-sufficient, you don't call another guy and leave with him on the back of his bike and take a road trip with him! Who does that?<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/uQ20Jsm" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380417966ra/827210.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And Woods? What the hell happened, man? It was like some alien invaded Woods body and made him clingy, needy and so f*ckin' annoying. Where the hell did the real Woods go? I want a sensitive hero, sure, but there is sensitive and then there is OTT, clingy sensitive. Woods became the latter, okay? Not even his dirty talk can save him because even that was an epic fail.<br><br>Exhibit A<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"Ah, that's good, baby. So damn good. Take it deep. Oh, hell yeah, gag on it." His words came out thick and raspy.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Gag...what?<br><br>Exhibit B<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"No one touches my pussy. This is my pussy, Della," he said in a growl.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Um, yeah. Won't even explain that one. I know what he meant but it just came out wrong. Totally not sexy. *smh*<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/wfCiuCf" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380738873ra/3117515.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Truthfully, the only reason I didn't DNF this book was because most of my GR friends who've read it ahead of me said something big happened at around 85% or 86%. I wanted to know what happened. So sue me. And when I finally did know what happened I wanted to do this...<br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=358sy02" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380738873ra/3117516.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And this...<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/6zln2SK" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380738873ra/3117517.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And this...<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/cPdvDFh" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380738873ra/3117518.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But then I realized that all of those things are not really good for my health, so I just did this...<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/fRLs8sk" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380738873ra/3117519.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Yeah. Not real healthy either but hey, what can I do? It happened. I didn't want it to happen but I'm not the author. The author can pretty much do what she wants, right? <br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/ES9Oaf0" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380434499ra/876990.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I mean, here's thing. I'm not upset because of what happened to that character. I get it. Sometimes authors employ this certain plot device if it's essential to moving the story along. I mean, GRR Martin is famous for this, and I get it. But what pissed me off was the fact that this "THING" happened in order for another character to get his own book and jump-start his story, which is totally unnecessary, IMO!<br><br>And contrary to what publishers (I'm assuming the publishers are pushing for more books) think, not every character deserves a f*ckin' book!! Some characters are better off as side characters!! These two characters were well loved already. There was no need to mess with that! It was already good. The fans are satisfied. Just leave it be! Huhuhu! They should have just left it alone. <br><br>But they didn't. I felt manipulated. Ugh! And as for Tripp's story? <br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/foFHfGX" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380434498ra/876988.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Sorry. I don't even know if I'll read Grant's story anymore. It's just the same old tactics all over again. Readers are actually smarter than that. I get that there is a huge market for these types of stories but you can only do so much with what flimsy plot you have. Without a strong plot and relatable characters, there is no point in continuing this farce. <br><br>I don't begrudge Abbi Glines for writing these stories. She's good at it, and As I have said, I've enjoyed them in the past. Yes, she tends to be formulaic but for me, as long as the execution is spot on and we get likable and strong characters, I'm okay with formulas. But what I'm not okay with is churning out book after book without more or less the same plot and the same old characters. It becomes boring and tedious. And that's just plain wrong.<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/t9UuCOK" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380417966ra/827213.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>

<div id="review_548149352" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/548149352" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/548149352?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer548149352" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18135827649841343065"><b>4 Stars!!!!</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/f7a8211e-59cd-4d33-a888-ae759aeb6277_zpsfe875130.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380411461i/808227.jpg' alt=' photo f7a8211e-59cd-4d33-a888-ae759aeb6277_zpsfe875130.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><i>Simple Perfection</i> starts off right where <i>Twisted Perfection</i> leaves off. Woods Kerrington is now solely responsible for his family’s country club. He is dealing with his grieving mother, his crazy ex, and the stress is getting to him. Thankfully, he has Della. The only thing keeping him together, keeping him sane. <br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/07127ff7-7505-485a-ae99-163b2ab17856_zpsad884171.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380411461i/808228.jpg' alt=' photo 07127ff7-7505-485a-ae99-163b2ab17856_zpsad884171.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Della is happy with Woods. For the first time in her life, she feels normal, special, loved. But she also feels that she’s undeserving of someone like Woods. Due to h</span>
  <span id="freeText18135827649841343065" style="display:none"><b>4 Stars!!!!</b><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/f7a8211e-59cd-4d33-a888-ae759aeb6277_zpsfe875130.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380411461i/808227.jpg" alt=" photo f7a8211e-59cd-4d33-a888-ae759aeb6277_zpsfe875130.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>Simple Perfection</i> starts off right where <i>Twisted Perfection</i> leaves off. Woods Kerrington is now solely responsible for his family’s country club. He is dealing with his grieving mother, his crazy ex, and the stress is getting to him. Thankfully, he has Della. The only thing keeping him together, keeping him sane. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/07127ff7-7505-485a-ae99-163b2ab17856_zpsad884171.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380411461i/808228.jpg" alt=" photo 07127ff7-7505-485a-ae99-163b2ab17856_zpsad884171.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Della is happy with Woods. For the first time in her life, she feels normal, special, loved. But she also feels that she’s undeserving of someone like Woods. Due to her family’s history, she thinks he deserves better than her. Someone who doesn’t have issues and who doesn’t have the possibility of becoming crazy like her mother. She can’t stay with him and hold him back.<br><b>
  <blockquote>How could we make this work? This couldn't be forever. I wanted this forever but Woods deserved so much more.</blockquote>
</b><br>No matter what the couple goes through, and they go through a lot, Woods knows Della is it for him. He never sees Della as damaged or a hindrance. To him, she is perfect. She’s the only thing he wants or needs and he will do whatever he has to do to protect her. <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>"She's my perfection. She holds my heart in her hands. When she hurts it brings me to my knees. There is no way to explain to you the way I feel about her. Just understand that I will not allow anyone to hurt her again. I won't forgive that. I lose a piece of my soul when I see her in pain."</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br>Woods is one of my favorite of Abbi’s guys, and my definite favorite of the Rosemary beach series. Not only is he sexy as hell, alpha with a bit of a dirty mouth <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <i><b>"Gonna come. Your hot little mouth wants it, doesn't it? My naughty baby wants it down her throat. Fuck yeah. That's my mouth to fuck." </b></i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but he is kind, compassionate, patient and loving. Pretty much the perfect guy! He loves Della fiercely. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/7087402c-8a9e-430a-943e-31577b0ad7ef_zps2cdec867.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380411461i/808229.jpg" alt=" photo 7087402c-8a9e-430a-943e-31577b0ad7ef_zps2cdec867.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Della is lost throughout this book. She needed to get away to find herself and figure things out. It was nice to get more of Della’s background and see her move on from her past and get over some of her fears. Being away from Woods made her realize how much she loves him, needs him, and wants to be with him. Once Della realizes she won’t only bring Woods down, that he is the anchor that grounds her, she is able to face him again. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/a08f7fc9-978e-4fa9-aa13-41065125125e_zpsb2ae8dfd.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380411461i/808230.jpg" alt=" photo a08f7fc9-978e-4fa9-aa13-41065125125e_zpsb2ae8dfd.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>
  <blockquote>"I want to be the strong one sometimes. I don't always want to be the weak one."<br>"I just want you. In whatever way I can have you."</blockquote>
</i> Just as things are starting to get back to normal for the couple, something big happens that shakes everyone on Rosemary beach. Tore my heart right from my chest. I understand that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This happened to set up Tripp’s book.... but seriously WHY WHY WHY!!?!??!?!? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I was still devastated. For all the times Woods has comforted and taken care of Della, she has to be the strong one for him now. <br><i>
  <blockquote>She was my glue right now. Being able to touch her was keeping me together.</blockquote>
</i> Della is there for Woods when she needs him. She will do anything she can for him, be everything he needs her to be. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/256c261c-1f7b-46cc-8733-c3603572226e_zpsfd00e7f0.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380411462i/808231.jpg" alt=" photo 256c261c-1f7b-46cc-8733-c3603572226e_zpsfd00e7f0.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Even though I was heart broken for a while,I was still very happy with the ending. The gas station. Woods makes me swoon like no other. Even though we don’t get an epilogue, it’s okay. I know we will catch up with these two in Grant’s and Tripp’s book down the road! <br><br><br>I adore Woods, and Della’s journey was wonderful to read about. I wanted a bit more closure with the whole Angelina/Wood’s mother thing. That bugged me a little. Maybe in another book, who knows? Although I didn’t love this book quite as much as the first, it was still a great read. Looking forward (even if I am a bit nervous) about Grant’s book! <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/ba0805bc-b8b0-45ae-8aa4-6958543c9a07_zpsf0d95a69.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380411462i/808232.jpg" alt=" photo ba0805bc-b8b0-45ae-8aa4-6958543c9a07_zpsf0d95a69.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="18135827649841343065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer582828432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6248614560709602120"> <b>4 Healing Stars!! </b><br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380416538i/822865.jpg' width='450' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>	<br/><br/>After the death of Wood’s father, he inherited everything and is now controlling the company, the same one he was once willing to give up his life in sacrifice for it. <br/>Well, not anymore. <br/>Della still has a lot of problems to overcome, but if Woods will have to choose, we will always choose Della. He will fight for her until the end. <br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380416538ra/822866.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Della will have a lot to overcome in this book, and she is settled in solving their problems and finally be the woman Woods deserves. <br/>But her qu</span>
  <span id="freeText6248614560709602120" style="display:none"> <b>4 Healing Stars!! </b><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380416538i/822865.jpg" width="450" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">	<br><br>After the death of Wood’s father, he inherited everything and is now controlling the company, the same one he was once willing to give up his life in sacrifice for it. <br>Well, not anymore. <br>Della still has a lot of problems to overcome, but if Woods will have to choose, we will always choose Della. He will fight for her until the end. <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380416538ra/822866.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Della will have a lot to overcome in this book, and she is settled in solving their problems and finally be the woman Woods deserves. <br>But her quest is only starting and there’ll be a lot of new discoveries and obstacles… being one of the biggest obstacles herself. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380416538i/822867.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Unfortunately, although this was a damn good reading, I didn’t like it as much as the previous one. <br>Woods is real great (Rush’s still my favorite, though.) and Della is also good in this book and very supportive of Woods in everything he has to go through… but there was some things that made give a lower rating. <br>Basically, (Don’t read the spoilers if you haven’t read this yet!) the obvious plot twist to introduce another spin-off with Tripp. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Was it really necessary to kill Jace?? Was it, Abbi??? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>And the knowledge that the first Grant's book <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[will end in a cliff-hanger. F*ucking Nan! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Nonetheless, this book hooked me up since the first pages, like all the books written by this woman, and I’ll will now wait anxiously for the next one, especially after the sweet ending. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I love how it ended in the gas station, just like their story started. So cute ;) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>Go read this people. This is probably one of the best NA series of the moment. </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_726013273" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/726013273" />
    <a title="Jen " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5962787-jen"><img alt="Jen " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563496869p2/5962787.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/726013273?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen " href="/user/show/5962787-jen">Jen </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5962787-jen?shelf=ya-na">ya-na</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5962787-jen?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5962787-jen?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer726013273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14378639682508220201"><b>2.5 Underwhelming Stars</b><br/><br/><i>
  <b>"Right now he needs you, I get it. But, Della, you started this journey to live life. Don’t forget that. You left one prison; don’t find yourself in another."</b>
</i><br/><br/>I’m going to keep this review short and “meh” because every road I can think to take leads to spoiler town and that’s not what I’m trying to accomplish. I love the fact that Della took some time to find her inner strength. I wish she would’ve gone about it in a different manner, but the finished product was a stro</span>
  <span id="freeText14378639682508220201" style="display:none"><b>2.5 Underwhelming Stars</b><br /><br /><i>
  <b>"Right now he needs you, I get it. But, Della, you started this journey to live life. Don’t forget that. You left one prison; don’t find yourself in another."</b>
</i><br /><br />I’m going to keep this review short and “meh” because every road I can think to take leads to spoiler town and that’s not what I’m trying to accomplish. I love the fact that Della took some time to find her inner strength. I wish she would’ve gone about it in a different manner, but the finished product was a stronger, more rational and mature Della. No complaints there. What the hell happened to Woods, though? I know he went through a whole lot during the course of the story, but he didn’t seem to handle any of the situations in typical “Woods” form. The bitches that ended up creating havoc in both he and Della’s lives were never really handled AND he turned into a freakishly clingy version of his former self. That behavior makes sense towards the very end of the story but not before then. Whether his sense of responsibility was so great he turned into a clinger, I can’t say. All I know is I didn’t enjoy reading it. <br /><br />This book took a turn for the worse for me at the 85% mark. It just seemed like drama for the sake of drama and I really think Ms. Glines missed the mark. To me it felt like needlessly sacrificing a part of the legacy that is this series simply to set up another book and it was done in a matter of a page or two. I didn’t mind the last 10% of this book being used to set up the next two books of the series, but this added little bit of heartache at the end didn’t work for me.<br /><br />After all of my bitching, I still enjoyed this story overall. And after everything’s said and done, we still have Woods and his filthy, dirty mouth to enjoy.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>”Gonna come. Your hot, little mouth wants it, doesn’t it? My naughty baby wants it down her throat. Fuck, yeah. That’s my mouth to fuck.”</b>
</i></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer548192659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16999646940347791408">I was really looking forward to another book about Woods and Della especially since I enjoyed the first book so much. I only have one question....What in the heck happened? <br/><br/>The Woods we knew and loved is G-O-N-E! Instead we have someone who cannot even function unless Della is around him every single minute! I understand he's concerned for her and that she makes him feel better but Woods was the one guy who had his act together. I hated that it was taken away. <br/><br/>Now let's talk Della...you just kne</span>
  <span id="freeText16999646940347791408" style="display:none">I was really looking forward to another book about Woods and Della especially since I enjoyed the first book so much. I only have one question....What in the heck happened? <br><br>The Woods we knew and loved is G-O-N-E! Instead we have someone who cannot even function unless Della is around him every single minute! I understand he's concerned for her and that she makes him feel better but Woods was the one guy who had his act together. I hated that it was taken away. <br><br>Now let's talk Della...you just knew there would be something that would cause some drama and IMO it was pretty lame. And even lamer was the whole thing Braden helped her with...seriously, THAT solved all her problems? Just like that? Nope, not buying it. <br><br>And who knew that all it took was Alabama with a gun to get rid of a certain someone....really? Too bad it didn't work on Nan! ;)<br><br>Of course, there is the kicker...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380298466ra/684232.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I call "foul"! I just hate when this happens. I really hate it when there could've been an easier way...it makes it seem like a cheap shot. :(<br><br>But it does set things up for Tripp...I guess I have to be careful about what I wish for! <br><br>And that's the other thing, all these storylines were taking over Woods and Della's story! Tripp's and then Grant's - please, please...I don't want to hear the details about Nan! <br><br>The few moments of happiness involved my favorites - Rush, Blaire and Nate. I loved every moment of "them". And I got a big kick out of the way Dean was acting. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380756556ra/3120114.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I did love the ending....that was <i>simple perfection</i>. I loved how Woods set that up.<br><br>Next up is <i>Take A Chance</i> with Grant...and hopefully not too much of you know who! (maybe if I keep saying it??) <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380756556i/3120115.jpg" width="400" height="070" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Favorite quotes: <br><br>♥ “You’re my all-in, Della. I’ll throw it all away for you."</span>
  <a data-text-id="16999646940347791408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_586320613" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/586320613" />
    <a title="Natasha is a Book Junkie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9389992-natasha-is-a-book-junkie"><img alt="Natasha is a Book Junkie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585046882p2/9389992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/586320613?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natasha is a Book Junkie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natasha is a Book Junkie" href="/user/show/9389992-natasha-is-a-book-junkie">Natasha is a Book Junkie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9389992-natasha-is-a-book-junkie?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9389992-natasha-is-a-book-junkie?shelf=natasha">natasha</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer586320613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11547146957587861099"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Our chapter was over. It was the most beautiful chapter in my life. I knew I’d had the happy ending way before it was time and now I had to live the rest of the story without him.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>Brace yourselves because Abbi Glines is armed and dangerous in this second instalment of the Perfection series and she is taking no prisoners. I was on pins and needles throughout most of this book, absorbing all the emotional curveballs being thrown at me and just when I thought it was safe to relax and b</span>
  <span id="freeText11547146957587861099" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Our chapter was over. It was the most beautiful chapter in my life. I knew I’d had the happy ending way before it was time and now I had to live the rest of the story without him.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Brace yourselves because Abbi Glines is armed and dangerous in this second instalment of the Perfection series and she is taking no prisoners. I was on pins and needles throughout most of this book, absorbing all the emotional curveballs being thrown at me and just when I thought it was safe to relax and breathe easy again, she did the unthinkable and dismantled my heart into a million little pieces. Have some tissues ready, maybe a bottle of wine nearby, and get ready for another rollercoaster ride that is guaranteed to leave you wobbly at the knees.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Hold her for me. Hold her tight. Don’t let her be lonely. Don’t let her hurt. Please.”</i>
</blockquote><br>In Twisted Perfection, Della and Woods have finally realised that they are stronger together than they are apart and have emotionally committed to one another and to a future together. But one tragic event in Woods’ life shakes the foundations of their young relationship and forces them to confront a reality that neither of them wished to face so soon. Having to deal with the aftermath of his father’s sudden death and a mother who refuses to acknowledge the woman he loves, Woods is torn between his love and devotion for Della and his need to protect her from her past, and his new responsibilities as head of the Kerrington Country Club. He has not grieved the loss of his father, his grief too intermingled with anger for the suffering his father had caused Della, and has chosen to bottle his emotions in favour of taking care of Della and her fragile emotional state. Woods has put Della first in his life, over anything and anyone, that resolve putting only further strain on his already problematic relationship with his only remaining parent.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I won’t let you near Della nor will I put you before her. Understand that if you make me choose, I will choose her without a second thought.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Della feels safe and loved for the first time in her life. Woods’ demonstrative and overly protective personality is equally comforting as it is overwhelming, at times making her feel smothered by him and convincing her more and more each day that she is an unfathomable burden to him, only holding him back from living his life.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“What was I good for? He had to worry about me. I was weak and needy. I was one more thing for him to stress over. I wasn’t any help at all.”</i>
</blockquote><br>In an ultimate act of selflessness and love for the man she thinks she would end up destroying, Della walks away. From Woods. From Rosemary. From the only security she has known in her life. And so she begins her transformation from broken and frightened little girl always depending on others to hold her hand and try to fix her, to a woman standing on her own two feet, drawing strength from within rather than from others, and unafraid to fight for what she wants the most in life. With further insight into Della’s horrific childhood, we get a complete picture of the battle she has had to fight daily in her mind, her journey of healing being full of unexpected surprises, but the more she has to overcome, the more she grows stronger and more confident in herself.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“He wants you, Della.”<br>“Sometimes what we want isn’t what is best for us.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Woods and Della’s story has not been smooth sailing right from the beginning and it is laced with drama and heartbreak all the way to the end. The chemistry between them is so deliciously multilayered, one minute they are tenderly romantic and genuinely vulnerable towards one another, and the next an almost frantic passion overtakes them and they use that intense connection to communicate their fears, to comfort each other, and to heal one another.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“… I can’t live without Della. I can’t breathe. I can’t f*cking concentrate. I need her. Just her. I can do anything if I have her with me.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Ms Glines’ writing style remains unique and unquestionably effective. Short sentences, complex emotions under the guise of simplicity, and a method of story-telling that keeps aiming at the reader’s heart with what I’d like to call “peanut butter sandwich” moments (hint: Rush and Blaire in Fallen Too Far) – simple scenes that are deceivingly ordinary but capable of stinging like an electric bolt. This is the conclusion to Woods and Della’s passionate story and it is everything I hoped it would be.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Love should be simple. I wasn’t simple.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380382869i/740934.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="http://www.natashaisabookjunkie.com/2013/09/23/simple-perfection-abbi-glines/" rel="nofollow noopener">See this review on my blog!</a> | <a href="http://www.facebook.com/natashaisabookjunkie" rel="nofollow noopener">Follow me on Facebook!</a> | <a href="http://www.twitter.com/natashabkjunkie" rel="nofollow noopener">Follow me on Twitter!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11547146957587861099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads"><img alt="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380942477p2/4197769.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/640401422?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" href="/user/show/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads">Jacqueline&#39;s Reads</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads?shelf=4-star-books">4-star-books</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer640401422" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8947434148294866537"><a href='http://imgur.com/75Kh7g7' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380425239i/848499._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>4.5 Give-Me-More-Woods Stars<br/><br/>** SPOILER FREE **</b><br/><br/>If you love Woods, then you will love Simple Perfection.<br/><br/>Simple Perfection is book 2 of the Perfection series, and book 5 of the Rosemary Beach series.<br/><br/><b>Series order:</b><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/491458723' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fallen Too Far</a> (Too Far, #1 | Rosemary Beach, #1) < ---- Read, 4 Stars<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/554927568' rel='nofollow noopener'>Never Too Far</a> (Too Far, #2 | Rosemary Beach, #2) < ---- Read, 3 Stars<br/><br/>Forever Too Far (Too Far, #3 | Rosemary Beach, #2) < ---- TBR<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/556996120' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twisted Perfection</a> (Perfection, #1 | Rosemary Beach, #4) < --- Read, 5 Stars<br/><br/>Simple Perf</span>
  <span id="freeText8947434148294866537" style="display:none"><a href="http://imgur.com/75Kh7g7" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380425239i/848499._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>4.5 Give-Me-More-Woods Stars<br><br>** SPOILER FREE **</b><br><br>If you love Woods, then you will love Simple Perfection.<br><br>Simple Perfection is book 2 of the Perfection series, and book 5 of the Rosemary Beach series.<br><br><b>Series order:</b><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/491458723" rel="nofollow noopener">Fallen Too Far</a> (Too Far, #1 | Rosemary Beach, #1) &lt; ---- Read, 4 Stars<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/554927568" rel="nofollow noopener">Never Too Far</a> (Too Far, #2 | Rosemary Beach, #2) &lt; ---- Read, 3 Stars<br><br>Forever Too Far (Too Far, #3 | Rosemary Beach, #2) &lt; ---- TBR<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/556996120" rel="nofollow noopener">Twisted Perfection</a> (Perfection, #1 | Rosemary Beach, #4) &lt; --- Read, 5 Stars<br><br>Simple Perfection (Perfection, #1 | Rosemary Beach, #5) &lt; ---- Read, 4.5 Stars<br><br>I loved Twisted Perfection. I loved it so much, I purchased a paperback copy and so when Simple Perfection came out, I couldn’t wait to read it. I think this would have been a five star read for me, if Abbi focused more on the Woods and Della dynamics, than the other Rosemary characters (which some readers love, so this is a personal thing for me).<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/Q2UW1SM" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380425239i/848500.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Della will piss you off. She will be irrational and slightly crazy. Again, I know there are readers who LOVE this, so there you have it. The best part of this book was Woods. Oh god, my love for Woods. He’s SO ALPHA! If you looked up Alpha in the dictionary, you will see his name (some readers may be turned off by this, so just so you know, the whole alpha thing is turned up a notch). I love alpha, sexy, I-Love-my-woman, woods. DAMN.<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/dFAx88q" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380425239i/848501.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Sigh. SWOON. FAINT, I love Woods. BAD.</b><br><br>For me, it’s very tricky on keeping me engaged in the second book of any series. Where can the characters go? The beginning picks up right where Twisted Perfection left off. So, Woods is dealing with his family and there’s plenty of drama on that side to keep you interested. I liked reading the parts about Woods’ mother and ex-girlfriend. Who doesn’t love a cat fight?<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/gcYuhU6" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380425239i/848502.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>It wasn't the way life was supposed to be, but it was my life. And I'd had Woods in it. That made it all okay.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Then there’s Della and her issues. I understand the direction Abbi was going and you do feel bad for Della. Do you agree with her? I am not sure, but it adds nice tension to the book.<br><br>Simple Perfection isn’t a light hearted read. It’s emotional and dramatic. If you are like me and LOVE Woods, then there’s no question, you need to read Simple Perfection. <br><br>For more reviews, visit <a href="http://jacquelinesreads.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Jacqueline's Reads</a></span>

<div id="review_548316606" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/548316606" />
    <a title="DKristin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6655835-dkristin"><img alt="DKristin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495583446p2/6655835.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/548316606?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="DKristin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="DKristin" href="/user/show/6655835-dkristin">DKristin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6655835-dkristin?shelf=own-a-copy">own-a-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6655835-dkristin?shelf=highly-anticipating">highly-anticipating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6655835-dkristin?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6655835-dkristin?shelf=dirty-thirty-month-reads">dirty-thirty-month-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer548316606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1985899848395589813">I'm sort of at a loss for words right now. I have said before that Abbi Glines books are like mashed potatoes -- comfortable, something you know, and love. I didn't really enjoy the Vincent Boys/Brothers all that much but other than that I liked the Too Far series and most of the Seabreeze series was solid, as well as her paranormal series. When I read Twisted Perfection I thought OMG Abbi has finally upped her game, I thought that book was wonderful. I loved Della, I loved Woods, I loved them t</span>
  <span id="freeText1985899848395589813" style="display:none">I'm sort of at a loss for words right now. I have said before that Abbi Glines books are like mashed potatoes -- comfortable, something you know, and love. I didn't really enjoy the Vincent Boys/Brothers all that much but other than that I liked the Too Far series and most of the Seabreeze series was solid, as well as her paranormal series. When I read Twisted Perfection I thought OMG Abbi has finally upped her game, I thought that book was wonderful. I loved Della, I loved Woods, I loved them together and I was super happy that they were going to get a second book. I was highly anticipating it as a matter of fact. Now having read it... I just have no words for how disappointed I am by this piece of crap!!! It wasn't absolutely awful but somehow Della managed to turn into this extremely insecure dumbass, Woods seemingly was suffering from Dissociative Identity Disorder and was either this overly alpha possessive type or crying like he forgot where he left his balls. Now don't get me wrong there were some emotional parts to this book and if he didn't have some sort of reaction to it that would have been a problem but it's the other times I am referring to. <br><br>Glines managed to write almost every single one of my most major pet peeves in one book! That's note worthy in and of itself!!! Firstly, we have a huge and major problem that could have been easily fixed with <b>one</b> 5 minute conversation but then carries on for a great deal of the book. Secondly, I felt like she saw some things that have been popular in recent books and decided to make it work for these characters whether it fit into how she created them to be or not. Third, we have someone who has experienced a traumatic life and exhibits signs of PTSD but somehow with new information and three weeks she is able to become almost completely "healed", and there were no Jesus sightings as far as I know!!! Fourth, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ senseless death!!! While I am glad that we got the info. on what the fuck was up with Bethy acting batshit out of nowhere and randomly I thought it made absolutely <b>NO SENSE</b> to kill off Jace due to Bethy being a dumbass! It was obviously just done to set up her and Tripp's book and like a vegan at an all meat buffet I don't get down like that!!! It would have made more sense for her to go the love triangle route if she needed to create drama. But having him dead, then Bethy is all broke up still about having an abortion, and Tripp is back and not going anywhere 5 years later... I just don't give a fuck! Even the scene was absolute garbage!!!! She just la-la-la's out into the ocean after a few shots of tequila and Jace has time to force Woods to take Bethy but they can't figure out a way for him to pull him out too, at least out of the current and if it were so strong how was he able to get Bethy to Woods??? I'm not usually this particular but if you're going to go there than it should make absolute and total sense! This is 5 years later not 5 weeks or even 2 or 3 years later how has Bethy managed to stay alive this long if she has always had this death wish? I'm just supposed to believe because she doesn't deserve Jace in her eyes that is what triggered this behavior? Whatevs!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Fifth, all of the re-capping!!! If someone is reading this book and hasn't at least read the book before it then I don't know what to tell you, but I don't enjoy reading a bunch of what happened in previous books that I've already read all over again. <br><br>For all the potential this story had I am so sad that it was this disappointing!!! I still want to read Grant's book and I still feel like Because of Low and Twisted Perfection were really AWESOME books... but IDK if my relationship with Abbi is going to make it much longer if this is the type of crap that I am expected to pay $3-$8 a pop for... <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380411486ra/808329.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="1985899848395589813" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/599651178?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelena" href="/user/show/7096828-kelena">Kelena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7096828-kelena?shelf=must-read">must-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7096828-kelena?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7096828-kelena?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7096828-kelena?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer599651178" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12949636911675984496"><b>Bazillion Rosemary Bittersweet Stars</b> <br/>Oh <b>Abbi Glines</b> indeed delivered <b>Woodella</b> Roller-Coaster Ending!<br/><br/>~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*<br/><i>
  <b>“I just want you. In whatever way I can have you..... Because you make my life amazing.”</b>
</i><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380419014ra/830186.gif' width='400' height='529' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Ahhhh......<br/>did I Cry? <b>You Bet!</b><br/>did I Laugh? <b>YES!</b><br/>did I found myself melting with <b>Woodella</b> steam? <b>*not in the <br/>room right now.... ran for a cold shower.</b><br/>did I Swoon? Add <b>Squeeing.... Sighing... Fainting....</b> into <br/>that question too..<br/>did I Like the ending? <b>LIKE IS ONE HELL`VA UND</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12949636911675984496" style="display:none"><b>Bazillion Rosemary Bittersweet Stars</b> <br>Oh <b>Abbi Glines</b> indeed delivered <b>Woodella</b> Roller-Coaster Ending!<br><br>~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*<br><i>
  <b>“I just want you. In whatever way I can have you..... Because you make my life amazing.”</b>
</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380419014ra/830186.gif" width="400" height="529" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ahhhh......<br>did I Cry? <b>You Bet!</b><br>did I Laugh? <b>YES!</b><br>did I found myself melting with <b>Woodella</b> steam? <b>*not in the <br>room right now.... ran for a cold shower.</b><br>did I Swoon? Add <b>Squeeing.... Sighing... Fainting....</b> into <br>that question too..<br>did I Like the ending? <b>LIKE IS ONE HELL`VA UNDERSTATEMENT ABOUT HOW MUCH I FUCKING LOVE THIS BOOK!</b><br><br>~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*<br><i>Simple Perfection</i> is floating with perfect amount of every heartfelt emotion that a book needed to be imprinted not in just your minds but also in your hearts too.<br><br>We all met <b>Della &amp; Woods</b> in <i>Twisted Perfection</i> and their <br>tale started from where we'd left them in <b>TP</b>.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380419014i/830187._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="550" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After Woods Kerrington father's sudden death he has the sole ownership of the family's country club. The very club his grandfather made sure will be Woods's when either he turned 25 or if his father dies, but Mr Kerrington always made an impression that Woods had to earn it and by doing so he has to marry Angelina. <br><br>Della tried to be supportive in any way she can to help Woods <br>with his father's death and his mother grieving. She was happy that she's there for him to stand beside him and have a life she always dreamed of.<br><br>But when you have witches like Angelina and Woods mother in <br>the picture you have see your beloved characters going through shit that'll make their lives miserable and you feel the urge to just dive into the frigging book and sort it all.<br><br>So, the obstacles started taken place and doubts sprouting the roots in Della's mind that she's never going to enough for Woods, that she'll end up crazy and hold him back from his thriving future.....<br><br><br>On the other hand Woods was keeping her on his palms, he treated her like a glass princesses, always making sure that she didn't fade away in the darkness that hunt her from the past, he always there for her when she needed him. She was <b>IT</b> to him or the way he says <b>Go-All-In</b>. <br><br>The doubts in Della's mind made her take the step of her life that <br>tore Woods heart but it's not like she was immune to it. Being apart from Woods made her realized that her love for him is endless and she needs him in her more then she needs to breath.<br><br>The Alpha in Woods wanted to run like hell and move heaven<br>and earth to bring his woman back because it was hard for him to imagine a life with his Della not in it.<br><br><i>
  <b>“Della was my go-all-in. She was my winning hand. <br>You can’t play when you go all in and lose. I’m out.”</b>
</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380419014i/830188._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="570" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>And what little misunderstanding made her do that turned out to be way better in her favour, she was mostly lost through this book but once the puzzles of her past started sorting out, she found her way to the light she was seeking throughout her life... the moment she realized that she's strong enough to be the anchor for Woods the way he was her's, she's ready to walk on the water to claim her man back!. <br><br><i>
  <b>I had always felt safe with Woods. That wasn’t new. <br>But now . . . now I felt like I’d found my anchor.</b>
</i><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380402675ra/782821.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Right when they were in the grasp of their <br><b>Unicorns &amp; Rainbows</b> a heartbreaking tragedy had hit <b>Rosemary</b> residents that`d changed everyones life. To be honest I didn't see that coming, in fact I still don't believe it! <br><br>The horrors Della had fought all her life were started looming over Woods, he was afraid that he'll be fade into the darkness. But this <br>time it was Della who turned out to the anchor for him to hold on tight.<br><br><b>
  <i>I couldn't have made it without her. Holding<br>her reminded me that I was alive.</i>
</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380419014ra/830189.gif" width="400" height="195" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*<br>I was hoping for a little epilogue but still I loved the way their story ended, can't picture anything else for their HEA, gonna say just one line.<br><b>The Gas Station</b> <br>I would love to read more about them in <b>Grant &amp; Tripp's</b> books. <br><br>The way <b>Abbi Glines</b> bring all her characters in one world through different books is quite amazing. I can't find enough words to appreciate her writing skills. She knows how to make her readers connected to each character and made them fall for all the positive aspects and hate the villain. <br><br>That's what you call the <b>BEST AUTHOR OF ALL TIMES!</b> <br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380419014ra/830190.gif" width="400" height="196" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer12625270623153725512"><b> 4/5 stars </b><br/><br/>THe first half of the book was (sorry!) frustrating to me. Woods was fine, it was Della who frustrated me so much. In the first book, I never pegged her as someone so weak as she is in this one!<br/>She was too nice, she gave into her fears way too easily, and ran away without finding out the reason of a huge misunderstanding.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380420691ra/834813.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Because of the big stupid misunderstanding, Woods and Della were separated for a big part of this book!<br/><br/>THe second half gets much better though. We finally find out wh</span>
  <span id="freeText12625270623153725512" style="display:none"><b> 4/5 stars </b><br><br>THe first half of the book was (sorry!) frustrating to me. Woods was fine, it was Della who frustrated me so much. In the first book, I never pegged her as someone so weak as she is in this one!<br>She was too nice, she gave into her fears way too easily, and ran away without finding out the reason of a huge misunderstanding.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380420691ra/834813.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Because of the big stupid misunderstanding, Woods and Della were separated for a big part of this book!<br><br>THe second half gets much better though. We finally find out what Della's terrors were.<br> I read so many statuses around 80% that they were sad and had to stop for a while. So I got extremely worried expecting something horrible to happen!! Well I raised the bar so high that when I read I didn't shed a tear.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380420691ra/834814.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>No, that's not what's supposed to make you cry. But something else does. Oh boy, does it come out of nowhere. I still can't believe it happened. I'm at a loss for words. <br>major major spoiler --&gt; <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Jace, who has been with us through 5 books, all the sudden gone, is just heartbreaking. Am I also supposed to blame Bethy?? I still have no clue why she was in the ocean drunk..Was she trying to commit suicide??<br>Just so many questions. Jace will truly be missed by all of his friends and family. And Bethy has a lot of regrets to get over. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380420691ra/834815.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>As for Nan... She wasn't really in this one, she was just mentioned, she didn't even have dialogue. But I have to get this off my chest. <br>Everyone in groups are saying she shouldn't end up with Grant (I agree). BUT that she should end up with Blaire's half brother. I'm sorry but I'm just going to be a bitch and just say I want her to end up alone. I think she's not good enough for Blaire's brother (I forgot his name) either. and Freakin' Grant you defended her one time STOP ITTTTTTT NOW! She's going to keep fucking you over<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380420691ra/834816.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>and Nan you better stop getting your claws into Grant, stop being so possessive over everything you can't have, just fucking-<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/593194.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Wood and Della do get their HEA I don't know if they will get another book, it didn't end with a cliffhanger.<br><br>But I am super eager to read Harlow and Grant's story (IT BETTER BE HARLOW AND GRANT)<br><br>*no cheating in this book whatsoeverrrrrrrrrrr!</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

This is not just a story about their love, this is Della's story of overcoming her fears and facing th</i></span>

This book was fantastic, it was fucktastic... It was FAN-FUCKING-TASTIC. It was candy for my eyes. <br><br>GAH! Why aren't my thinking things working?????</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380393724ra/758086.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><i>Woods has found his girl, the one that owns him, owns his soul. His all-in. But Della has demons of her past and too many fears for their future to fully trust in the fact that she will ever be what he needs. This is not just a story about their love, this is Della's story of overcoming her fears and facing them. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380418855i/829727.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This is Woods' story of learning to let go just a bit and finding someone that loves him as strongly as he loves them. <br><br>There are far too many things that happened in this story to avoid giving anything away. I will say that if you have read the prior books, you have a little overlap in the story, but reading this particular scene, is like reading it for the first time. <br><br>And the way Woods loves this girl is so flippin' sweet. Brace yourselves, because Woods is going to weaken you knees, dampen your panties and leave you completely breathless. </i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380418855i/829728._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>

Just understand that I will not allow anyone to hurt her again. I won't forgive that. I lose a piece of my soul when I see her in pain."<br><br>"With Woods's arms wrapped around me and the beat of his heart pressed against my chest, I knew he would hold me steady. If I ever fell, I'd have him to catch me."</b></i> </blockquote><br><br>Now, this book is certainly not all hearts and flowers. Della has a lot of issues she needs to sort out and this takes time. But Abbi Glines masterfully guides you through her journey. And it's not just a story that focuses on Della and Woods, you get a lot of the guys of Rosemary. I am so happy to know we still have two more books coming our way for Grant's story. There is no way I am ready to say goodbye to all of these characters. A brilliant and well crafted series that had you loving hard. <br><br>There is one particular part in this story that shocked me, I had held myself together pretty well during the angst of Della &amp; Woods, but this. This, brought me to my knees. My heart still fucking hurts right now. I don't know if I want to hug Abbi Glines for throwing something so unexpected at us - that truly turned this story into something so much greater or punch her in her face.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418855ra/829729.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/568802.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418855ra/829730.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>There is a moment towards the end of this book that just felt like a bunch of kids realized that their youth was over - that they were growing up. Long gone were the days of just having fun on the beach. Innocence of youth drifted off to sea. <br><br>When I came to the final chapters of this book, this was fluttering though my head. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380418855i/829731.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1040990148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8671378940401879009"><i>
  <b>"In all her twisted perfection she had made me fall helplessly in love with her. A life without her in it seemed pointless."</b>
</i><br/><br/>No words can describe what I'm feeling right now. I am sooo in love with <b>Woods Kerrington</b> and this perfect sequel of the Rosemary Beach. Honestly, I did not immediately delve into this book after reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17333880.Twisted_Perfection__Perfection___1_' title='Twisted Perfection (Perfection, #1) by Abbi Glines' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twisted Perfection</a> because I didn't enjoy Woods and Della's story that time.<br/><br/>But this book-- *sigh* It's surprisingly better. It was just so good! The love story did aff</span>
  <span id="freeText8671378940401879009" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"In all her twisted perfection she had made me fall helplessly in love with her. A life without her in it seemed pointless."</b>
</i><br /><br />No words can describe what I'm feeling right now. I am sooo in love with <b>Woods Kerrington</b> and this perfect sequel of the Rosemary Beach. Honestly, I did not immediately delve into this book after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17333880.Twisted_Perfection__Perfection___1_" title="Twisted Perfection (Perfection, #1) by Abbi Glines" rel="nofollow noopener">Twisted Perfection</a> because I didn't enjoy Woods and Della's story that time.<br /><br />But this book-- *sigh* It's surprisingly better. It was just so good! The love story did affect me because there were too many feels in it. The drama was a little bit exaggerated but who cares? You can't just fall out of love with Woods once you're already hooked with him. ;)<br /><br />In this book, not only was Della and Woods' story highlighted. There was a glimpse of Jace and Bethy's, too. As well as Blaire and Rush, Grant, and of course my baby Tripp's. :) I loved how these characters converged together and molded their friendship.<br /><br />There was something in this book that made me cry-- especially at the end. And although I was already spoiled on that certain "twist", still, I couldn't help but cry. Damn. Abbi Glines. Why???<br /><br />But for the main story, it was good. It was a sweet, happy conclusion for Della and Woods' story. I could not ask for a better ending!<br /><br />Rating: 5 Stars</span>

<div id="review_727514372" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/727514372" />
    <a title="Vallsykes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5164414-vallsykes"><img alt="Vallsykes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1367067514p2/5164414.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/727514372?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vallsykes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vallsykes" href="/user/show/5164414-vallsykes">Vallsykes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Abbi Glines &amp; NA</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5164414-vallsykes?shelf=sequels-are-lame">sequels-are-lame</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5164414-vallsykes?shelf=wtf-conflict">wtf-conflict</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5164414-vallsykes?shelf=rewrite-the-ending-or-plot-issues">rewrite-the-ending-or-plot-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5164414-vallsykes?shelf=can-t-believe-his-mouth">can-t-believe-his-mouth</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5164414-vallsykes?shelf=been-there-read-that">been-there-read-that</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5164414-vallsykes?shelf=almost-3-but-not-quite">almost-3-but-not-quite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5164414-vallsykes?shelf=young-adult-erotica">young-adult-erotica</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5164414-vallsykes?shelf=new-adult-rave">new-adult-rave</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5164414-vallsykes?shelf=annoying-or-repetitive-language">annoying-or-repetitive-language</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5164414-vallsykes?shelf=weak-or-shy-heroine">weak-or-shy-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer727514372" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15408058166903807304"><b>2.5 stars</b><br/>This rating may get upped to 3, but for now I say this...<br/><b>Negatives:</b><br/>a. <u>too much formula without finesse</u>--parents are effed up and manipulative, angst from trauma of past abuse, boy-meets-girl, but boy's ex or relative is a she-bitch who hates his girl, girl runs away- and so this formula is getting played, especially when...<br/>b. <b>
  <u>the plot is not fleshed out enough</u>
</b>, where pertinent conflicts are left unresolved, H/h development as a couple is weak after the final "this is it; let's BE to</span>
  <span id="freeText15408058166903807304" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars</b><br />This rating may get upped to 3, but for now I say this...<br /><b>Negatives:</b><br />a. <u>too much formula without finesse</u>--parents are effed up and manipulative, angst from trauma of past abuse, boy-meets-girl, but boy's ex or relative is a she-bitch who hates his girl, girl runs away- and so this formula is getting played, especially when...<br />b. <b>
  <u>the plot is not fleshed out enough</u>
</b>, where pertinent conflicts are left unresolved, H/h development as a couple is weak after the final "this is it; let's BE together" and mini-surprises/cliffhangers replace falling resolution so that readers are prematurely seduced into reading the NEXT story.[<b>Just finish the damn story already!</b>]<br />c. One more thing...dirty talk. I'm all for the <i>"You're mine. Mine. Mine."</i> during sex, but sometimes, just let the hero say it another way. And <i>“Ah, that’s good, baby. So damn good. Take it deep. Oh, hell yeah, gag on it”</i> is NOT sexy to me. Just sayin' LOL<br /><b>Positives:</b><br />a. Despite my exasperation with gimmicks, <u>I really like the author's creation of setting and characters</u>. Sometimes I even like the dialogue.<br />b. I think <u>Glines has a good hand at writing NA genre</u>. She can do plot formulas well with addition to adding her own spin of moods and hot young alphas. Maybe she'd do better by strengthening her falling resolution and ending of plot, eventually.<br />c. For me, Glines has some alright stories, tales of young love which can be pleasing and fleetingly smutty, but in a NA way. LOL<br /><br />Woods and Della get an HEA of sorts, but some telling conflicts they face aren't dealt with fully before the plot hurls the reader into a major conflict that is a set up for other characters' stories. <br /><br />I would like a solid story instead of a book where the story rushes "what happens after" and relies on "to be cont'd" by-lines. I get that this is all the rage these days, but it makes me, the reader, feel unsatisfied.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15408058166903807304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
